1.0 INTRODUCTION
This report presents the Traffic Impact Study (TIS) prepared by DKS Associates (DKS) for the
proposed Box Springs Road Apartments, Tentative Tract Map No. 35414 (proposed project)
located on the southeast corner of Clark Street/Box Springs Road in the City of Moreno Valley
(City). The proposed project would develop 240 apartment units.
This TIS has been prepared based on the Scoping Agreement for Traffic Impact Study approved
by the City of Moreno Valley Transportation Engineering Division (located in Appendix A) and is
consistent with the policies of the City of Moreno Valley General Plan Circulation Element and the
guidelines of the Riverside County Traffic Impact Analysis Preparation Guide (July 2004).

Purpose of the TIS and Study Objectives
The purpose of this TIS is to evaluate the traffic and circulation impacts of the proposed project.
The study objectives of this TIS include:
        1. Documentation and analysis of existing traffic conditions in the vicinity of the project
           site.
        2. Evaluation of the traffic impacts of the proposed development on the street network in
           the vicinity of the proposed project.
        3. Assessment of project access and internal circulation
        4. Determination of additional circulation system features and system management
           actions needed to achieve the City's level of service (LOS) requirements with
           implementation of the proposed project.

Site Location and Study Area
The proposed project would be developed on a vacant site that is surrounded by existing
residential uses to the north, State Route 60 (SR 60) to the south, and vacant land to the east and
west. The project site is located on the southeast corner of Clark Street/Box Springs Road. The
project site location and study area are shown on Figure 1.
Regional access would be provided by SR 60 and Interstate 215 (I-215) and with interchanges
located within a mile of the project site. Local access would be provided by Box Springs Road and
Day Street.
Per the Scoping Agreement approved by the City, the project study area consists of the following
eight (8) study area intersections:
        1.       I-215 northbound ramps/Box Springs Road
        2.       Sycamore Canyon Road/Box Springs Road
        3.       I-215 southbound ramps/Box Springs Road
        4.       Clark Street/Box Springs Road
        5.       Day Street/Box Springs Road ­ Ironwood Avenue
        6.       Day Street/SR 60 westbound ramps
        7.       Day Street/SR 60 eastbound ramps
        8.       Project Driveway/Box Springs Road

Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                       Page 1
Traffic Study Analysis Scenarios
Per the Scoping Agreement, the following traffic scenarios were analyzed in this TIS:

Existing Traffic
Due to the current closure and reconstruction of the SR 60/Box Springs Road interchange, existing
peak hour traffic volumes for the study area were obtained from previous traffic studies and from
the City of Riverside's traffic data base. These existing traffic counts ranged from March 2003 and
2005 counts. These volumes were then updated with a two (2) percent annual growth rate. In
addition, the volumes at SR 60/Box Springs Road ramps as well Sycamore Canyon Road/Box
Springs Road were adjusted to account for the reconfiguration of the ramps. The volumes at Day
Street/SR 60 ramps were also balanced to reflect the volumes at Day Street/ Box Springs Road.

Opening Year 2012 Baseline Condition
It is estimated that the proposed project would be completely built and fully occupied by year 2012
(minimum five year horizon per City guidelines). Baseline traffic in this scenario was projected to
2012 by increasing the existing (adjusted) 2007 traffic volumes by an annual growth rate of two (2)
percent per year as stated in the Scoping Agreement. In addition to the growth rate increase, data
containing approved/pending projects in the study area was provided by the City and was used in
the evaluation of the Opening Year 2012 Baseline Condition.
The pending projects include projects that are proposed and in the review process, but not fully
approved. In addition, the Opening Year 2012 scenario includes all future roadway and
intersection improvements on the City's Capital Improvement Projects (CIP) list and/or mitigation
measures of approved development projects (if any).

Opening Year 2012 with Project
Traffic in this scenario was developed by adding the trips generated from the proposed project to
Opening Year 2012 Baseline traffic conditions. This scenario was the basis for determining
project-specific impacts and mitigation measures for the short-term condition.

General Plan Buildout Condition
Per the Scoping Agreement, the intersection of Day Street/Box Springs Road ­ Ironwood Avenue
was analyzed for the General Plan Buildout conditions (with and without project). General Plan
Buildout Baseline volumes were obtained from the City's Traffic Forecast Model. Project traffic at
that intersection was added to the baseline volumes and then analyzed for potential impacts in the
Buildout condition.




Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                       Page 3
2.0 PROJECT DESCRIPTION
The following section provides information on the construction and permanent operation of the
proposed project relative to the local and regional circulation network.

Existing Project Site Land Use
The 12.4 acre project site is located south of Box Springs Road. The project site is currently
vacant and bounded residential uses to the north. State Route 60 (SR 60) freeway borders the
project to the south, and vacant land to the east and west.

Project Description
Exhibit 2 presents the site plan of the proposed project. The proposed project consists of the
development of 240 apartments. Based on information by the project applicant, the proposed
project would be completed and fully occupied by 2009.
Primary access to the proposed project would be provided at the existing signalized intersection of
Clark Street/Box Springs Road, with two full access unsignalized driveways located on Clark
Street, south of the signalized intersection. In addition, a full access driveway would be located on
Box Springs Road on the northeast corner of the property.

Existing and Proposed Land Use and Zoning
The project site is currently designated as Community Commercial (CC) in the General Plan. The
proposed project would require a zone change to R20 Residential (residential, up to 20 units per
acre). The proposed residential use would generate less vehicle trips than the current commercial
zoning.
Assuming a 0.3 floor-to-area ratio (FAR) for commercial zoning, the 12.4 acre project site would
yield approximately 162,000 square feet of retail/commercial uses. The Institute of Transportation
Engineers (ITE) Trip Generation, 7th Edition trip rates for Shopping Center were used to estimate
daily and peak hour trips of the currently zoned retail/commercial use for the site. Based on the trip
rates, the currently zoned 162,000 square foot shopping center would generate approximately
9,292 daily trips, 209 a.m. peak hour trips, and 861 p.m. peak hour trips.
In comparison with the proposed project (240 apartments), using ITE trip rates for Apartment, the
proposed project would generate approximately 1,613 daily trips, 122 a.m. peak hour trips, and 149
p.m. peak hour trips.
The proposed project would generate 7,679 less daily trips, 87 less a.m. peak hour trips, and 712
less p.m. peak hour trips than the currently zoned retail/commercial uses on the project site.
Therefore, the proposed residential use would generate less vehicle trips than the current
commercial zoning.




Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                          Page 4
3.0 EXISTING STUDY AREA CONDITIONS
The following section describes the existing traffic conditions in the project study area. Due to the
partial-closure of the SR 60/Box Springs Road Interchange for its improvement project at the time
of this TIS, existing a.m. and p.m. peak hour traffic counts were obtained from various sources.
These sources included the City of Riverside and counts from traffic count firms (Counts Unlimited
and Southland Car Counters). Data from these sources were from 2003 and 2005 pre-closure.
With approval from the City Traffic Engineer, DKS adjusted those traffic counts to 2007 conditions
assuming a conservative two (2) percent annual growth rate, and also re-adjusted the volumes to
be consistent with the new interchange configuration and geometrics (partial diamond westbound
ramps and eastbound hook-ramps on to Sycamore Canyon Road, south of Box Springs Road.

Roadways
The following describes the existing roadways in the study area.

State Route 60
State Route 60 (SR 60) is an eight-lane (four lanes in each direction, including carpool lanes) east-
west State freeway facility that would provide regional access to the project site via interchanges at
Box Springs Road and Day Street. In the project vicinity, Interstate 215 (I-215) has its northern
junction with SR 60. Currently, freeway and interchange improvements are being constructed at
the SR 60/I-215 interchange. SR 60 originates in the downtown Los Angeles area to the west, and
terminates at its junction with Interstate 10 (I-10) in the Banning-Beaumont area of Riverside
County.

Interstate 215
Interstate 215 (I-215) is a six-lane (three lanes in each direction) north-south State freeway facility
in the project vicinity. In the project vicinity, I-215 has its northern junction with SR 60. Currently,
freeway and interchange improvements are being constructed at the SR 60/I-215 interchange. I-
215 originates in the project vicinity at its junction with SR 60, and terminates in the Murrieta-
Temecula area at its junction with Interstate 15 (I-15).

Box Springs Road
Box Springs Road is located north and adjacent to the project site and runs in the east-west
direction. Box Springs Road is a modified Minor Arterial that provides access to I-215 and SR 60
via Day Street. In the project vicinity, Box Springs Road is a three lane (two lanes in the
westbound direction and one lane in the eastbound direction) roadway with a divided painted
median that serves as a two-way left-turn lane (TWLTL) for existing commercial uses along the
street. The proposed project would construct the second eastbound lane along its frontage of Box
Springs Road. East of the project site, Box Springs Road becomes a four lane divided roadway
that provides access to SR 60 via Day Street. Box Springs Road would provide access to the
project site via its intersection with Clark Street and an unsignalized driveway on Box Springs
Road.


Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                            Page 6
Day Street
Day Street is located east of the project site and runs in the north-south direction. Day Street is
designated as a divided Arterial in the City General Plan. In the project vicinity, Day Street is a four
lane roadway (two lanes in each direction) with a painted median. Day Street would provide local
access to the project site.

Traffic Controls and Intersection Geometrics
Figure 3 illustrates the study area's existing traffic controls and intersection geometrics. As shown,
all study area intersections are currently controlled by traffic signals.

Traffic Volumes
Existing peak hour traffic volumes for the study area were obtained from March 2003 and 2005
counts prior to the partial-closure of the interchange for the construction of improvements. Existing
counts were obtained for the intersection of Clark Street/Box Springs Road in May 2007. At the
direction of the City Traffic Engineer, these volumes were then updated with a conservative two (2)
percent annual growth rate consistent with the City's general growth rates (except for Clark
Street/Box Springs Road). Then, the volumes at Box Springs Road and I-215 Ramps, as well at
Box Springs Road and Sycamore Canyon Road were adjusted for the reconfiguration of the ramps
to its current configuration. Finally, the volumes at all intersections were balanced to reflect the
updated volumes and interchange configuration. Figure 4 presents the existing 2007 a.m. and
p.m. peak hour traffic volumes in the study area. The raw peak hour intersection turn movement
count worksheets can be found in Appendix B.

Levels of Service
The following section discusses the methodology utilized to determine intersection levels of service
(LOS) and summarizes the results of existing condition LOS analysis.

Methodology
The assessment of intersection conditions in this TIS addresses LOS in terms of vehicle control
delay (in seconds per vehicle) for signalized and unsignalized intersections. The level of service
grades (LOS A-F), as reported in Highway Capacity Manual (HCM2000), are dependent on the
volume-to-capacity (V/C) ratios and vehicle control delay (in seconds) at the signalized and
unsignalized intersection, respectively. Both signalized and unsignalized study area intersections
have been analyzed using the HCM2000 method. The TRAFFIX (version 7.8) software was used
to determine intersection LOS. TRAFFIX is consistent with the HCM2000 methodologies.
The degree of congestion at an intersection is described by the level of service, which ranges from
A to F, with A representing free-flow conditions with little delay, and F representing over-saturated
traffic flow throughout the peak hour. A complete description of the meaning of level of service can
be found in the Transportation Research Board Special Report 209, Highway Capacity Manual
(HCM2000). Brief descriptions of the six levels of service, as abstracted from the HCM, are shown
in Table A.



Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                            Page 7

   of        Intersection               Intersection
                                                                                       Description

 (LOS)       (in seconds)               (in seconds)
                                                                No approach phase is fully utilized by traffic, and no
                                                                vehicle waits longer than one red indication. Typically,
  A                10                          10
                                                                the approach appears quite open, turns are made
                                                                easily, and nearly all drivers find freedom of operation.
                                                                This service level represents stable operation, where
                                                                an occasional approach phase is fully utilized and a
  B             > 10 ­ 15                  > 10 ­ 20
                                                                substantial number are nearing full use. Many drivers
                                                                begin to feel restricted within platoons of vehicles.
                                                                This level still represents stable operating conditions.
                                                                Occasionally drivers may have to wait through more
  C             > 15 ­ 25                  > 20 ­ 35            than one red signal indication, and backups may
                                                                develop behind turning vehicles. Most drivers feel
                                                                somewhat restricted, but not objectionably so.
                                                                This level encompasses a zone of increasing
                                                                restriction approaching instability at the intersection.
                                                                Delays to approaching vehicles may be substantial
  D             > 25 ­ 35                  > 35 ­ 55            during short peaks within the peak period; however,
                                                                enough cycles with lower demand occur to permit
                                                                periodic clearance of developing queues, thus
                                                                preventing excessive backups.
                                                                Capacity occurs at the upper end of this service level.
                                                                It represents the most vehicles that any particular
  E             > 35 ­ 50                  > 55 ­ 80            intersection approach can accommodate. Full
                                                                utilization of every signal cycle is seldom attained no
                                                                matter how great the demand.
                                                                This level describes forced flow operations at low
                                                                speeds, where volumes exceed capacity. These
                                                                conditions usually result from queues of vehicles
                                                                backing up from a restriction downstream. Speeds are
  F               > 50                        > 80
                                                                reduced substantially, and stoppages may occur for
                                                                short or long periods of time due to the congestion. In
                                                                the extreme case, both speed and volume can drop to
                                                                zero.

Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                                             Page 10
Significance Criteria
The City of Moreno Valley has not yet prepared traffic study guidelines, so traffic studies are
generally prepared in accordance with the County of Riverside Traffic Study Guidelines with future
direction from the City Traffic Engineer as part of the City's Scoping Agreement process. The
significance threshold is based on the City of Moreno Valley General Plan Draft EIR (June 2005)
which states:
         LOS D is applicable to intersections and roadway segments that are adjacent to freeway
         on/off ramps, and/or adjacent land uses. LOS C is applicable to all other intersections and
         roadway segments. Boundary intersections are assumed to be LOS D.
In addition, according to Figure 5.2-7 of the City of Moreno Valley General Plan Draft EIR, all study
area roadways and intersections are shown to be designated to the LOS D standard.
According to the County of Riverside Traffic Study Guidelines, the significance level for
unsignalized intersections is that, once they are found to operate at LOS E or F, a traffic signal
warrant would be prepared to determine whether signalization of the intersections would be
appropriate. Therefore, if the project causes an intersection to operate below the minimum
standard, the project would cause a significant project-specific impact at that intersection, and
specific mitigation measures must be developed to improve the intersection's LOS back to
satisfactory levels.

Based on the analysis methodology described above, the existing a.m. and p.m. peak hour traffic
volumes were input into the TRAFFIX software to determine the existing LOS in the study area.

According to Table B, the existing study intersections are currently operating with satisfactory LOS
(i.e., LOS D or better) in the a.m. and p.m. peak hours.

Transit Service
Bus service in the project vicinity is provided by the Riverside Transit Agency (RTA). RTA
operates both local fixed-route and regional bus service within its service area. Routes 16, 16E,
and 208 currently service the study area with stops along Box Springs Road. The following
describes these routes and their operational characteristics.
Route 16 travels from downtown Riverside to March Air Reserve Base with stops along Box
Springs Road. It operates on weekdays and weekends with service in both directions. Route 16E
provides express service on the same route as Route 16 during the weekdays only. Route 208
travels from the Riverside Metrolink Station to Temecula with stops along Box Springs Road.
Route 208 provides service in both directions during the weekdays only.

Pedestrian and Bicycle Facilities
Currently, there are bike lanes along Box Springs Road. Pedestrian sidewalks are also provided.
Crosswalk and pedestrian phases are provided at traffic signals that would accommodate
pedestrian movements. Disabled ramps are also provided at the signalized intersections.

4.0 PROJECT TRAFFIC
This section describes the trip generation, distribution, and assignment of the proposed project's
traffic volumes in the study area.

Trip Generation
As noted in the Scoping Agreement, trip generation for the proposed project was developed using
trip rates provided in the Institute of Transportation Engineers (ITE) Trip Generation, 7th Edition. A
summary of the trip generation rates and resulting vehicle trips for the proposed project is
presented in Table C.
                                            Table C ­ Project Trip Generation Estimates

                                                                                               AM Peak Hour                    PM Peak Hour
 Land Use                                                   Size                Daily         In   Out   Total                In Out Total
 ITE Trip Rates 1
 Apartments                                             per     DU 2             6.72      0.10      0.41        0.51       0.40   0.22   0.62
 Trip Generation
 Proposed Project- Apartments                           240     DU 2           1,613         24        98         122        96     53    149
Source: Institute of Transportation Engineers (ITE) Trip Generation, 7th Edition, 2003 and Trip Generation Handbook, 2003


According to Table C, the proposed project would generate approximately 1,613 daily trips, 122
a.m. peak hour trips (24 inbound and 98 outbound), and 149 p.m. peak hour trips (96 inbound and
53 outbound).

Trip Distribution and Assignment
Project trip distribution patterns were based on factors such as: 1) location of housing and jobs
within the County of Riverside and adjacent Cities (Riverside, Corona, Perris, Murrieta, Temecula,
and San Jacinto), and Riverside, San Bernardino, and San Diego Counties; and 2) transportation
facility characteristics that impact travel demand (i.e. locations of urban arterials, freeways, and
interchanges). The trip distribution patterns shown in Figure 5 are based on the existing roadway
network in the study area.
To calculate the project traffic volumes at each study area intersection, project trips were
distributed through each intersection utilizing the generalized distribution percentages. The trip
distribution at each intersection was applied to the project's trip generation estimates (Table C) to
calculate the turn movement volumes at each study area intersection. Trip distribution and
assignment procedures were performed utilizing TRAFFIX. The resulting trip assignments at each
study intersection are shown in Figure 6.




Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                                                             Page 13
5.0 TRAFFIC ANALYSIS
This section assesses the future baseline and project-added traffic conditions under the different
analysis scenarios described previously: Opening Year 2012 Baseline Condition (without project);
Opening Year 2012 Baseline with Project; and General Plan Horizon Year 2025.

Opening Year 2012 Baseline Condition
According to the applicant, the proposed project would be fully completed and occupied by 2012.
An Opening Year 2012 Baseline Condition was based on the application of an annual growth rate,
as directed and approved by the City, and then applied to the existing peak hour traffic volumes
and the addition of the traffic generated by other approved and/or pending projects in the vicinity of
the project study area.

Growth Rate
Per consultation with the City Traffic Engineer and based on the analysis of the population and
socio-economic growth in the vicinity as shown in other approved traffic studies, an ambient annual
growth rate of two (2) percent per year was applied to the existing traffic. This resulted in a five-
year growth of ten percent (i.e., growth factor of 1.10) that was applied to the existing traffic
volumes.

Approved and Pending Projects
In addition to the growth rate, traffic volumes from approved and pending projects in the study area
were provided by the City and used in the evaluation of the Opening Year 2012 Baseline Condition.
The approved/pending projects include projects that are approved or proposed, and are in the
review process, but not constructed and fully operational. Figure 7 illustrates the locations of the
approved/pending projects. Traffic volumes with the forecast trips from this and other
approved/pending projects are located in Appendix D.

Traffic Volumes and Geometrics
As discussed, the two percent annual growth rate was applied to the existing intersection turn
volumes and the growth reflecting the peak hour volumes from the approved/pending projects were
added resulting in the year 2012 Opening Year Baseline traffic condition. The peak hour traffic
volumes at the study intersections for the Opening Year 2012 Baseline Condition (without project)
are presented in Figure 8.

According to Table E, the signalized study intersection of Day Street/Box Springs Road would
continue to operate with unsatisfactory levels of service (LOS F) with addition of the project during
both the a.m. and p.m. peak hours. Since this intersection is already forecast to operate with
unsatisfactory levels of service in the 2012 Baseline condition, the project would not create a
significant impact at this intersection. However, the proposed project would contribute to a
cumulative impact in the 2012 plus Project condition. Based on the table E, the proposed project
would contribute 4.8 percent of new traffic at this intersection during the impacted p.m. peak hour.
The Project Driveway at Box Springs Roads is also forecast to operate at an unsatisfactory level of
service (LOS F) in the p.m. peak hour. The LOS F movement is the northbound left turn vehicles
departing from the project site delayed by the eastbound and westbound through volumes on Box
Springs Road.

Mitigation Measures
The intersection of Day Street/Box Springs Road is forecast to operate with unsatisfactory levels of
service (LOS F) in the 2012 Baseline and 2012 plus Project conditions. The project would not
create a significant impact at this intersection since it would already operate at LOS F in the
baseline condition. However, the proposed project would contribute to a cumulative impact in the
2012 plus Project condition. The Project Driveway at Box Springs Roads is also forecast to
operate at an unsatisfactory level of service (LOS F) in the p.m. peak hour. This would be a
significant project impact.
The implementation of the mitigation measures defined below would achieve satisfactory levels of
service at these intersections:
MM TRAF-1:       The proposed project would contribute its fair-share cost of 4.8 percent to
                 future improvements to the Day Street/Box Springs Road intersection, or
                 other appropriate transportation improvement determined by the City.
                 Specific improvements that would mitigate the cumulative impacts at this
                 intersection include:
                                  -   Add a second (dual) northbound left turn lane.
                                  -   Provided Overlap phasing for the northbound right turn
                                  -   Add a second (dual) westbound left turn lane.
                 With these improvements, the intersection would operate at LOS D in both the
                 a.m. and p.m. peak hours of the 2012 Baseline and Baseline plus Project
                 conditions.
MM TRAF-2:       Restrict the Project Driveway/Box Springs Road intersection to right turn
                 in/out only access.
                 Installation of a traffic signal at this location would not be warranted as the
                 minimum minor street volume (on the Project Driveway) would not meet the
                 minimum volume threshold of 150 vehicles per hour on a single approach (based
                 on the Manual of Uniform Traffic Control Devices ­ MUTCD). The forecast
                 volumes on the minor street (Project Driveway) are 26 vehicles in the a.m. peak
                 hour and 15 vehicles in the p.m. peak hour. Also, since the right turn movements
Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                     Page 22
                 on the minor street are forecast to operate with satisfactory levels of service, the
                 delayed left-turning vehicles also have the opportunity to make the right turn
                 movement and use a different route to their destinations. These left-turning
                 vehicles can also use the signalized intersection at Clark Street/Box Springs Road
                 as an alternative route to their destination, which is forecast to operate with
                 satisfactory level of service (LOS B in the a.m. peak hour and LOS C in the p.m.
                 peak hour).

Project Fair-Share and Traffic Uniform Mitigation Fee
The Riverside County Board of Supervisors recognized the need to establish a comprehensive
funding source to mitigate the cumulative regional transportation impacts of new development on
regional arterial highways. The need to establish a comprehensive funding source for arterial
highway improvements has evolved into the development of the Transportation Uniform Mitigation
Fee (TUMF) for Western Riverside County.
In anticipation of the continued rapid future growth projected in Riverside County, several county
wide planning processes were initiated in 1999, which included: the Riverside County General
Plan Update, the Community Environmental Transportation Acceptability Process (CETAP), and
the Multi-Species Habitat Conservation Plan (MSHCP). Related to these planning processes was
the need to fund the mitigation of the cumulative regional transportation impacts of future new
development through the TUMF. Regional arterial highways in Western Riverside County are
forecast to carry significant traffic volumes by 2025. While localized fee programs exist to mitigate
the local impacts of new development on the transportation system in specific areas, and while
these programs are effective locally, they are disparate for meeting the regional demand for
transportation infrastructure. The Western Riverside Council of Governments (WRCOG) is the
responsible agency for the management of the Western Riverside County TUMF.
Therefore, as mandated in the Countywide adopted TUMF by the WRCOG, all new residential,
industrial, retail commercial, and service commercial developments are required to pay their fees
according to the Current WRCOG Transportation Uniform Mitigation Fee Increase Schedule.
Since the proposed project would contribute traffic volumes at one study intersection that is
forecast to continue to operate with unsatisfactory LOS with and without the project, the proposed
project would be required to contribute its fair-share costs to the City's approved funding
mechanism for future transportation improvements (i.e., Developer Impact Fees ­ DIF and/or
Traffic Uniform Mitigation Fee ­ TUMF).

General Plan Buildout Year 2025 Condition
Traffic Volumes and Geometrics
The Buildout Year 2025 a.m. and p.m. peak hour traffic volumes were obtained from City's General
Plan Travel Demand Model. Per the Scoping Agreement, Day Street/Box Springs Road - Ironwood
Avenue was analyzed per for the General Plan Buildout Condition. Appendix E contains the raw
data from the City's traffic model, and Figure 10 illustrates the 2025 baseline (without project) traffic
volumes at this intersection.


Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                         Page 23
It is important to note that the City's traffic model analyzed a Commercial land use on the project
site. The Commercial land use would generate more traffic than the proposed project. Assuming a
0.3 floor-to-area ratio (FAR) for commercial zoning, the 12.4 acre project site would yield
approximately 162,000 square feet of retail/commercial uses. The Institute of Transportation
Engineers (ITE) Trip Generation, 7th Edition trip rates for Shopping Center were used to estimate
daily and peak hour trips of the currently zoned retail/commercial use for the site. Based on the trip
rates, the currently zoned 162,000 square foot shopping center would generate approximately
9,292 daily trips, 209 a.m. peak hour trips, and 861 p.m. peak hour trips.
In comparison with the proposed project (240 apartments), using ITE trip rates for Apartment, the
proposed project would generate approximately 1,613 daily trips, 122 a.m. peak hour trips, and 149
p.m. peak hour trips.
The proposed project would generate 7,679 less daily trips, 87 less a.m. peak hour trips, and 712
less p.m. peak hour trips than the currently zoned retail/commercial uses on the project site.
Therefore, the proposed residential use would generate less vehicle trips than the current
commercial zoning.

Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                              Page 25
6.0 ON-SITE CIRCULATION, ACCESS, PARKING, AND
    ALTERNATIVE TRANSPORTATION
This section discusses the potential project-related impacts with respect to vehicular and
pedestrian on-site circulation, access, parking, and alternative transportation (pedestrian, bicycle,
and transit).

Project Access
Vehicular and Emergency Access
As currently planned, two full access driveways to the project site would are planned on Clark
Street with access to its signalized intersection at Box Springs Road. In addition, a secondary right
turn in/out access would be provided on Box Springs Road on the northeast corner of the project
site. Based on review of the project site plan, the design of the proposed project would allow for
adequate residential vehicular access and emergency access to the public roadways of Box
Springs Road and Clark Street, and therefore, no impacts would occur.

On-Site Circulation
The internal vehicular circulation system consists of internal roads with a loop-system and some
hammerhead turn around points at the ends of some drive aisles. According to the project site
plan, these internal roads would be constructed to be consistent with the City's drive aisle
standards (minimum 24 foot width). With the internal roadways designed to City standards, no
impacts related to the on site circulation for the proposed project would occur.

Parking
According to the City of Moreno Valley Municipal Code, the proposed project is required to provide
408 parking spaces. According to Table 9.11.040A-12, Off-Street Parking Requirements, of the
City's Municipal Code, one bedroom units are required to be parked at 1.5 spaces per unit, and two
bedroom units are required to be parked at 2.0 spaces per unit. One covered space per unit and
guest parking at 0.25 spaces per unit are included in the minimum parking standard.

Therefore, all 144 one-bedroom units are required to be parked at 216 spaces, and all 96 two-
bedroom units are required to be parked at 192 spaces, for a total on-site parking requirement of
408 spaces. Of the 408 spaces, 348 spaces would be dedicated to residents, while 60 spaces
would be dedicated as guest spaces. Of the 348 residential spaces, 240 spaces would be required
as covered parking spaces.

Based on review of the site plan, a total of 468 parking spaces would be provided on-site for the
proposed project, which would satisfy the City's Municipal Code's parking requirements.
Therefore, the parking spaces provided on the project site would be consistent with the City's
Municipal Code.




Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                     Page 28
Pedestrian and Bicycle Circulation
Currently, there are Class II (striped) bike lanes along Box Springs Road. Pedestrian sidewalks
are also provided along both streets. Crosswalk and pedestrian phases are provided at traffic
signals that would accommodate pedestrian movements. Disabled ramps are also provided at the
signalized intersections. The proposed project will construct their frontage with Box Springs Road
to the City's standards for sidewalks and bike lanes and will be consistent with existing facilities.
Therefore, with the project designed to City standards, there would be no impacts to pedestrian
and bicycle circulation with the proposed project.

Transit
Bus service within the vicinity of the project site is currently provided by the Riverside Transit
Agency (RTA). RTA operates both local fixed-route and regional bus service within its service
area. Routes 16, 16E, and 208 currently serve the study area. The RTA updates ridership
statistics every three months on all routes. When the ridership demand approaches the route's
capacity, additional buses are added to the route. Therefore, development of the proposed project
would not result in a significant impact to transit service in the project vicinity.

Mitigation Measures
The proposed project would not result in an impact related to vehicular and emergency access,
parking, pedestrian and bicycle circulation, or a significant impact related to transit service.
Therefore, no mitigation is required.




Box Springs Road Apartments TIS                                                                     Page 29

Intersection Level of Service Impacts
Opening Year 2012 plus Project
The signalized study intersection of Day Street/Box Springs Road would continue to operate with
unsatisfactory levels of service (LOS F) with addition of the project during both the a.m. and p.m.
peak hour in the 2012 Opening Year. Since this intersection is already forecast to operate with
unsatisfactory levels of service in the 2012 Baseline condition, the project would not create a
significant impact at this intersection. However, the proposed project would contribute to a
cumulative impact in the 2012 plus Project condition. The Project Driveway/Box Springs Road
intersection is forecast to operate at LOS F in the p.m. peak hour. This would be a significant
project impact.
The implementation of the mitigation measures defined below would achieve satisfactory levels of
service at these intersections:
MM TRAF-1:       The proposed project would contribute its fair-share cost of 4.8 percent to
                 future improvements to the Day Street/Box Springs Road intersection, or
                 other appropriate transportation improvement determined by the City.

                 intersection include:
                                  -   Add a second (dual) northbound left turn lane.
                                  -   Provided Overlap phasing for the northbound right turn
                                  -   Add a second (dual) westbound left turn lane.
                 With these improvements, the intersection would operate at LOS D in both the
                 a.m. and p.m. peak hours of the 2012 Baseline and Baseline plus Project
                 conditions.

                 in/out only access.
                 Installation of a traffic signal at this location would not be warranted as the
                 minimum minor street volume (on the Project Driveway) would not meet the
                 minimum volume threshold of 150 vehicles per hour on a single approach (based
                 on the MUTCD). The forecast volumes on the minor street (Project Driveway) are
                 26 vehicles in the a.m. peak hour and 15 vehicles in the p.m. peak hour. Also,
